http://big.dk/projects/zir/zir.html Great sustainable architecture by Danish Architect Bjarke Ingels. The Seven Peaks of Azerbaijan is a master plan for a Zero Energy resort and entertainment city on Zira Island situated within the Caspian Sea. Located within the crescent shaped bay of Azerbaijan's capital Baku, Zira Island is designed to be a sustainable model for urban development and an iconographic skyline recognizable from the city's coastline. The Seven Peaks of Azerbaijan proposes an architectural landscape derived from its natural landscape. The mountains are conceived not only as metaphors, but engineered as entire eco-systems, a model for future sustainable urban development.
Film: The Seven Peaks of Azerbaijan on Zira Island.  http://www.big.dk/projects/zir/zirmovie.html

Following the trend of bringing more green space to cities like Urban Gardening, Pocket Gardens and Green Roofs, Mothership came up with the idea of the Copy Garden.  A part of a nearby park or garden is literally copied into a non-green and often cheerless place in the urban environment. In front of the photo on vinyl real plants and shrubs are placed as found in the copied park. This phenomenon is also widely used in Chinese and Japanese cities. In the first Copy Garden in Rotterdam the trail is also extended, so that it looks like you can literally go through the "park". The natural vegetation in front of the photo wall and the continued path adds to the trompe l'oeil effect.  http://www.enterthemothership.com/nggallery/page-28/album-98/gallery-297/
Brei-Graffiti in Nieuwegein, The Nederlands On an early and very cold morning of December 1, 2010 a group of women lead by Marly Weemen of Mothership in Rotterdam yarnbombed De Krul ("the curl"), a work of art in the central market square in Nieuwegein. Hundreds of smaller knittted pieces was sewn together to make up the 40 m2 to cover De Krul.

The Rolling Bridge, located on the Paddington Basin in London, was created by Thomas Heatherwick. It is twelve meters long and opens every Friday at noon. Rather than a conventional opening bridge mechanism, consisting of a single rigid element that lifts to let boats pass, the Rolling Bridge gets out of the way by curling up until its two ends touch.  http://www.kuriositas.com/2010/03/rolling-bridge-that-curls.html

Robots of Brixton Robots of Brixton is a six-minute, visually stunning political allegory, showing humanoid robots' rage against a police state. Kibwe Tavares was inspired by class riots in his hometown of Brixton, England - but he knew that by representing one group of immigrants, he'd only exclude others who faced similar hardships. Slug Gone pure wool slug pellets are manufactured from the fleece of sheep. Wool fibres have very fine scales with small barbs on the tip called cuticle cells. These cause wool fibres to felt and matt together. Wool fibres are very hygroscopic and this plus the sand and grit already in the compound and the potassium salts from the sweat glands of the sheep absorb some of the slime from the slug's foot to cause irritation, resulting in the slug finding easier feeding methods.

Can one book change a life?  "I thought, if a woman can do this, I am also a woman so I can also write books and do things like her. That's what motivates me."-Okanta Kate, 17  
One e-book can change a life. It changed Okanta Kate's life forever. After reading The Shark by Ghanaian author Peggy Oppong -- a book Worldreader digitized and added to her Kindle, Okanta Kate was hooked, and magical things began to happen. This 17-year-old high school student has became an avid reader, and has devoured more than 100 books in one year. She's writing poetry and short stories, and aspires to not only achieve great things, but to inspire others around her to achieve great things as well.
Over 200 million children in sub-Saharan Africa have never read a book simply due to the fact that books never make it there. One non-profit is trying to change that.  More information:  (http://www.talknerdytome.net/2012/06/1-million-e-books-to-developing.html) Worldreader.org

DO NOT PANIC!!! ;-)  How to escape from an anaconda  An excerpt from the manual for the members of the Peace Corps, working in the Amazon jungle. 1. If you are attacked by an anaconda, do not run. It still moves faster. In any case, do not panic!  2. Lie on your back. Keep your legs together and keep your arms close to the body.  3. Press your chin against the chest.  4. The snake starts to crawl upon you.  5. Do not panic.  6. Observe the snake, it will begin to swallow your feet - an anaconda always starts with the feet. Let it swallow your feet and ankles. In any case, do not panic!  7. Then the snake starts to swallow you down. It takes a lot of time and all the time you will need to lie very still. Do not Panic!  8. When the snake have swallowed your legs to the knees, begin to act - slowly, trying to make as little as possible of unnecessary movements. Pull out a knife and very gently insert it into the side of the mouth of the snake. Then flick the knife and with a swift movement cut the snake's head off.  9. Always carry a knife.  10. The knife must be sharp.   Search engine Hotels and Tickets: http://otelibileti.ru/

Dindang natural building school is in a small village in Thailand called Paksong. The buildings at Dindang are made with a variety of natural building methods, among them bamboo wattle and daub, cob, adobe and palm thatching with decorative plaster designs, called pargeting, portraying the rainforest that surrounds the village. Unfortunately, as modern building methods were introduced in the Phato area, the traditional techniques of clay house building were largely forgotten. By setting up a natural building school, Dindang hopes to bring back the traditional building knowledge to the community to make life easy again.

For 30 years New Mexico-based architect Michael Reynolds ("The Garbage Warrior") and his green disciples have devoted their time to advancing the art of âEarthship Biotectureâ by building self-sufficient, off-the-grid communities where design and function converge in eco-harmony.  "The Simple Survival Model Earthship evolved from the very basic prototype we constructed in Haiti. The purpose of the original Haiti build was to reevaluate the concept of necessity. No matter how well the "developed world" Earthship prototypes worked, they were absolutely out of the budget of what could be achieved in Haiti. This caused us to take life itself to the basics and try to apply the globally proven Earthship concepts at a ground zero level. We succeeded... and in the end, we (the entire crew of nine) wanted to have one of these for ourselves. We wanted this unit not only because it functioned very well; but because it was very quick and inexpensive to build, thus leaving the owner with a life rather than a mortgage bondage for the next thirty years. This inspired the Simple Survival Model Earthship we are presenting here."  http://earthship.org/simple-survival

Nordic Folkecenter for Renewable Energy in Thy is constructiing an affordable passive house. The goal is to keep the price below 10,000 DKK per m2 including VAT. Passive house is a concept that originated in Germany but is now spreading to Denmark. At the moment there are only approximately 200 passive houses in Denmark, but Folkecenter wants to support the passive house movement by building a low-cost passive house, which is fully open to the public. The architect is Per Clausen from Moeller Nielsen Architects and the craftsmen are local people. The building materials are also, when possible, local.  Follow the construction and see more images on: http://www.folkecenter.net/gb/news/fc/affordable-passivehouse/  Nordic Folkecenter for Renewable Energy on Facebook: https://www.facebook.com/nordiskfolkecenter
Solar Cells for Schools in Burkina Faso Nordic Folkecenter for Renewable Energy has in cooperation with Association Kologh Naba, Burkina Faso in 2013 set up solar installations at 40 schools in off grid areas of Ouagadougou, the capital of Burkina Faso.  The installations are sponsored by Merkur Bank.  Merkur Bank: https://www.merkur.dk/uk/Home/tabid/348/Default.aspx Association Kologh Naba: http://www.kologh-naba.org/index.php?lang=en See Nordic Folkecenter for more photos; http://www.folkecenter.net/gb/news/fc/PV-Light-for-15-schools-in-burkina-faso/

REFUGEE AND ENTREPRENEUR!  What to take with you when you flee? 32-year-old Marial Parmena was not in doubt. He took his solar panel on his back as he fled from the fighting in Sudsudan, and carried it more than 400 kilometers to a refugee camp in Uganda.   Now he gets 30 eurocent for charging a cell phone in the refugee camp.  He earns approx. 6 euro per day.

Ramial Chipped Wood (RCW) - Bois RamÃ©aux FragmentÃ©s (BRF)  Wood chips make a good mulch for woody plants. To go a step further, you want to use ramial wood chips, which are wood chips made from the outer reaches of a deciduous tree. That means the smaller branches, including the leaves if possible, and not so much the trunk and thicker branches (the rule of thumb is nothing more than 2.5 inches thick). The term ramial is based on a french word, rameal, which means ârelated to the small branchâ. It was coined by the French Canadian, Prof. Gilles Lemieux, who pioneered the research.

The Danish documentary  "Days of Hope" ('Under den samme himmel) to be screened at the Film Festival "Cine Droit Libre" in Burkina Faso.  For the 10th successive year the Film Festival will take place in Ouagadougou, the capital of Burkina Faso. From June 1 to 7 cultural centers, universities, schools and squares in the capital are turned into a festival area. The aim is to create awareness and debate on Human Rights and Freedom of Expression through the medium of film.  The Festival is the biggest film festival on Human Rights and Freedom of Expression in West Africa, and the Danish Embassy in Burkina Faso support along with a wide range of other donors the festival - including notably "Movies that Matter".

An Open Letter to Join the Fashion Revolution  On 24th April last year, 1133 people were killed and over 2500 were injured when the Rana Plaza factory complex collapsed in Dhaka, Bangladesh - social and environmental catastrophes won't stop unless we act fast.  Fashion Revolution is about building a future where an accident like the Rana Plaza factory collapse never happens again. We believe knowing who made our clothes is the first step in transforming the fashion industry. Knowing who made our clothes requires transparency, and this implies openness, honesty, communication and accountability.   Itâs about re-connecting broken links and celebrating the relationship between shoppers and the people who make our clothes, shoes, accessories and jewellery â all the things we call fashion.    The huge success of Fashion Revolution Day globally this year, with tens of thousands of people turning an item of clothing #insideout and asking brands and retailers to tell them Who Made Your Clothes? is testament of how much was done to encourage transparency throughout the supply chain. #insideout was the no. 1 trend worldwide on Twitter on 24 April.  We couldn't have done this without you; and want to continue to use your power, people power, to fund our progress for 2015. We know that we have only scratched the surface this year and if we want to be bigger, stronger and better next year (and every year) we need funds.   Your money and your donations are our independence, the only way that we can operate freely, to say what we want and do what we want.   Of course, we are calling on brands and organisations to support us, but we want to be in a position to call our supporters our "partners" and not our "sponsors". That way we can maintain our unique voice, and follow our own agenda.  We have begged and borrowed to make Fashion Revolution Day happen; our team in the UK, and all other teams worldwide, have worked tirelessly - overtime and through the night, giving time, calling on all personal networks and contacts - and everything that you have seen so far, all the amazing support, all the initiatives, every single event, was initiated by passion and commitment.  Our Global Advisory Committee have all used their means and considerable influence to help us spread the word and create change, instigating events and encouraging support.  This is the first time in history that everyone who wants to see a more sustainable future for fashion has come together, and although Fashion Revolution Day is just one day a year, the Fashion Revolution movement now needs to grow, and keep asking the questions, because we don't have the answers - yet.   Please help us to make 2015 Fashion Revolution Day even more spectacular. With your help and your donations, we will reach further and wider, independently, and consolidate the incredible momentum that we have generated so far.   https://www.indiegogo.com/projects/fashion-revolution-a-global-movement#home

"Manual system made with recycled materials based on a pulley and crank, plastic caps tied to an "endless string" of nylon or polyethylene, as well as hydraulic hoses of pvc and other simple materials that facilitate the extraction of water from a deep well without the use of electricity, gasoline or diessel and with minimal effort. The caps function as Pistons, tubes like cylinders; the pulley can be done with a bicycle wheel in disuse and crank, welding three tubes at right angles..."

"Alberta artist, Peter von Tiesenhausen, has effectively stopped oil corporations from putting a pipeline through his 800 acre property by covering it with artwork and copyrighting the top six inches of his land as an artwork.  Von Tiesenausen decided to talk to them in their own language: Money. The copyright claim makes his entire property a work of art since he has covered it with visual art scupltures   The copyright also drastically increases the remuneration of around $200 for lost crops to around $600,000 for an " artistic property disturbance".  Dealing with the oil tycoons as a business man, he has also been able to cut down on their harassing phone calls and visits."  http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/05/30/1303087/-Artist-Stops-Oil-Pipeline-Cold  See Peter von Tiesenhausen's Artwork here: http://www.tiesenhausen.net/

Happy that I am not in Ouaga right now!  Originally I had planned to visit Burkina Faso in October-November this year to participate in the SIAO Craft Fair, which is held every second year in the capital Ouagadougou. This year it would run from today, Friday 31 October and throughout next week until Sunday, November 9th. However, the fair was cancelled a month ago due to the Ebola epidemic in West Africa. The authorities would not take the risk of 400,000 exhibitors and visitors from across Africa and Europe packed closely together in the exhibition halls with the danger of getting Ebola to the country and spreading it further around. I then decided to postpone my visit until after Christmas, which is also a better time for me.  In light of the events in Ouagadougou in recent days, I am glad that I am not there now. There have been massive demonstrations and there are reports of five dead and 60 wounded. A man was killed yesterday by a stray bullet just around the corner from the guest house "Chez Giuliana" where I would have stayed.   Here's a report from Ouaga: http://www.ilfattoquotidiano.it/2014/10/30/in-burkina-faso-dove-colpo-alle-porte-fuori-proiettili-rabbia/1180896/

Light over Africa - New Book by Folkecenter August 2015 Published by: Nordic Folkecenter for Renewable Energy, Denmark  DKK 85 (EUR 12) + Shipping Hardback, 64 pages B5 (176 Ã 250 mm) ISBN: 978-87-7778-002-8 Publication date: Aug. 2015  Brief: Over the years Folkecenter has transferred renewable energy know-how around the globe; it has organized solar lighting projects in Africa since 1998. By 2015 Folkecenter in cooperation with local NGOâs and suppliers has installed solar systems in over 300 rural schools in Mali, Uganda and Burkina Faso in the villages less than 5 % of the people have access to electricity. In the book, Light over Africa, you will find the background of the solar lighting projects, the impact for the local people, the keys to success and the next challenge: a plan for solar lighting in 10 000 village schools in the above-mentioned 3 African countries. Here two thirds of the populations are illiterates; in the countryside even more. With the implementing of the new plan 2 million village inhabitants (10 000 schools, each 200 students) will have the opportunity to attend evening school to learn to read and write. The investment will be EUR 10 million (EUR 1 000 for each school). Weaving modern cloth with Victorian loom  When Daniel Harris rescued a rusting loom from an old barn in rural Wales, it led to the creation of London's first micro-mill.  Established in 2011, the London Cloth Company uses traditional weaving techniques and a range of equipment dating all the way back to the 1870s. Three years on, the company supplies woven cloth to a growing number of designers, companies and individuals.

THE WAVE  In spring 1967, in Palo Alto, California, history teacher Ron Jones conducted an experiment with his class of 15-year-olds to sample the experience of the attraction and rise of the Nazis in Germany before World War II.  In a matter of days the experiment began to get out of control, as those attracted to the movement became aggressive zealots and the rigid rules invited confusion and chaos.  This story has attracted considerable attention over the years through films, books, plays and musicals, and verges on urban legend.  It serves as a teaching tool, to facilitate discussion of those uncomfortable topics of history, human nature, psychology, group behavior, intolerance and hate. The primary purpose of this website is to document and separate fact from fiction about the original experiment.  As the story is told and re-told, reported and fictionalized, Video: https://youtu.be/ICng-KRxXJ8  Read more: http://www.thewavehome.com/

Pedal-Powered âUn-knittingâ Machine   Make do and unmend? Meet the âun-knittingâ machine, a pedal-powered apparatus designed to recycle unwanted knitwear. The curious contraption is the brainchild of Imogen Hedges, a London-based product-and-furniture designer who discovered that charity shops sometimes spend hours unraveling sweaters by hand. âThey can make more money out of selling the wool than they can from the sweaters,â says the Kingston University graduate, one of a select group of student designers exhibiting at the The National Centre for Craft & Design this month.  YARN AGAIN Built around an old bicycle frame, Hedgesâs machine requires little more than a well-oiled pair of legs to run. The âun-knitterâ sits on a chair on one end, unraveling the garment as itâs pulled along the circumference of the wheel. Wool, which retains its elasticity better than other fibers, works best, as do knits derived from continuous lengths of fiber. To eliminate kinks, the yarn passes through the steam of a electric kettle. Finally, it finds its way to a hand-cranked spindle, where itâs rewound into a ball for re-knitting.

In line with the Piccard Family tradition of scientific exploration and protection of the environment, Solar Impulse wants to demonstrate that clean technologies can achieve impossible goals. The record breaking solo flight of 5 days and 5 nights without fuel from Nagoya to Hawaii gives a clear message : everybody could use the planeâs technologies on the ground to halve our worldâs energy consumption, save natural resources and improve our quality of life. This message is being spread by the pilots to the general public, students, key decision-makers and entrepreneurs all over the world.

Then when you land it is like a jump back into the PAST.  Most cars are still polluting. Most houses are still bad insulated.  Most technology is old."

SOCIAL FRIDGES In Argentina, more and more "social fridges", installed in the street offer free meals to people who approach it. There's even one in the famous Plaza de Mayo, in front of the presidential palace in the heart of Buenos Aires.  How to explain this phenomenon?  This, at least in part, is a way to meet the increasing poverty in the country. Since 2001 NGOs or organizations like Catholic Relief Services have opened soup kitchens, that is to say, free restaurants or food distribution centers, as there are in France for the poor. But a few years ago, a restaurateur had the idea of installing a refrigerator on his sidewalk and to store cooked food in individual trays wrapped in cellophane that passersby could withdraw freely. Food that would otherwise have ended in the trash, was now available to people in need. Anyone could use it without being asked anything.  This has been successful and others have copied the concept in several parts of the country, especially in front of public hospitals in poor suburbs where, clearly, many of those who come for free treatment also struggle to support themselves with food. In reality, the concept of "social fridges" comes from Germany, where they are longstanding. But it is true that these street refrigerators have multiplied in recent months in Argentina following the increased number of people in need  During the last two years of the presidency of Cristina Kirchner, living conditions have worsened for many Argentines, especially because of inflation. According to the indicator of the Catholic University, considered the most reliable, at the end of 2015, 29% of the population lived below the poverty line. And during the first three months of this year, that percentage has increased nearly 5 points,.

According to the just released Global Slavery Index the number of people living in "modern slavery" has increased by 28% in two years, from 35.8 million in 2014 to 45.8 million today.  "Incidences of slavery were found in all 167 countries in the index, with India home to the largest total number with an estimated 18.4 million slaves among its 1.3 billion population.  But North Korea ranked as worst in terms of concentration with one in every 20 people - or 4.4 percent of its 25 million population - in slavery and its government doing the least to end this with reports of state-sanctioned forced labour. "Hair embroidery is a particular technique practiced by lay Buddhist women to create devotional images. The embroiderers used their own hair as threads and applied them on silk to stitch figures. Scholars contend that this tradition started from the Tang Dynasty (618-907). However, the resurgence of this practice in the Ming period (1368-1644) was related to two historical factors: the spread of the cult of Guanyin, the most prevalent Chinese female deity, and the proliferation of embroidering Guanyin during late imperial China. In recent works on womenâs talent, scholars have cursorily mentioned hair embroidery, but they have failed to study it in detail. Hair embroideries of Guanyin offer us a felicitous window on this tradition. Hair embroidery was a unique site where women externalized part of their body to communicate with Guanyin.  Hair embroidered Tapestries by Yuan Miao. Since the time of the Tang Dynasty, hair has been used to embroider sacred tapestries, which transmit the wisdom of spiritual leaders through generations. This video will take you to a remote town in the plains of southern China where you can witness the creation of these beautiful spiritual embroideries featuring the art of Yuan Miao, a dakini and zen master, and traditional Guanyins."  Source: New Century Foundation www.newcenturyfoundation.org
